To implement the requested solution, we will break down the task into several components, each responsible for a specific part of the functionality. The main components will include:

1. **WhatsApp API Integration**: A class to handle interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
2. **Database Management**: A class to manage storing and retrieving call and message data.
3. **Automated Reply System**: A class to handle sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
4. **Web Dashboard**: A Flask-based web application to provide a real-time log view and CSV export functionality.
5. **GUI Application**: A Tkinter-based GUI to allow users to interact with the system.

### Core Classes and Functions

1. **WhatsAppAPI**: 
   - `send_message(phone_number, message)`: Sends a message to a specified phone number.
   - `receive_message()`: Listens for incoming messages and logs them.

2. **DatabaseManager**:
   - `log_call(caller_info, timestamp)`: Logs call information with a timestamp.
   - `log_message(message_info, timestamp)`: Logs message information with a timestamp.
   - `export_to_csv()`: Exports logs to a CSV file.

3. **AutomatedReplySystem**:
   - `send_automated_reply(caller_info)`: Sends an automated reply to a missed call.
   - `schedule_message(phone_number, message, time)`: Schedules a message to be sent at a specific time.

4. **WebDashboard**:
   - `run_dashboard()`: Starts the Flask web server for the dashboard.
   - `get_logs()`: Retrieves logs for display on the dashboard.

5. **GUIApplication**:
   - `start()`: Initializes and runs the GUI application.

### Implementation

#### main.py

```python
'''

Main entry point for the missed-call text-back solution.

'''

from whatsapp_api import WhatsAppAPI
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem
from web_dashboard import WebDashboard
from gui_application import GUIApplication

def main():
    # Initialize components
    whatsapp_api = WhatsAppAPI()
    db_manager = DatabaseManager()
    reply_system = AutomatedReplySystem(whatsapp_api, db_manager)
    dashboard = WebDashboard(db_manager)
    gui_app = GUIApplication(reply_system, dashboard)

    # Start the GUI application
    gui_app.start()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

#### whatsapp_api.py

```python
'''

Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.

'''

class WhatsAppAPI:
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        # Code to send a message via WhatsApp API
        print(f"Sending message to {phone_number}: {message}")

    def receive_message(self):
        # Code to receive messages from WhatsApp API
        print("Listening for incoming messages...")
```

#### database_manager.py

```python
'''

Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.

'''

import csv
import datetime

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []

    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")

    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")

    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)

            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

#### automated_reply_system.py

```python
'''

Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.

'''

import datetime
import threading

class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager

    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())

    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

#### web_dashboard.py

```python
'''

Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.

'''

from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file
import threading

class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.app = Flask(__name__)

        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})

        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)

    def run_dashboard(self):
        threading.Thread(target=self.app.run, kwargs={'debug': True}).start()
```

#### gui_application.py

```python
'''

Provides a GUI application for user interaction.

'''

import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox

class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard

    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()

        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")

        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)

        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)

        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)

        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")

        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)

        root.mainloop()
```

```python
'''
Main entry point for the missed-call text-back solution.
'''
from whatsapp_api import WhatsAppAPI
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem
from web_dashboard import WebDashboard
from gui_application import GUIApplication
def main():
    # Initialize components
    whatsapp_api = WhatsAppAPI()
    db_manager = DatabaseManager()
    reply_system = AutomatedReplySystem(whatsapp_api, db_manager)
    dashboard = WebDashboard(db_manager)
    gui_app = GUIApplication(reply_system, dashboard)
    # Start the GUI application
    gui_app.start()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

```python
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        # Code to send a message via WhatsApp API
        print(f"Sending message to {phone_number}: {message}")
    def receive_message(self):
        # Code to receive messages from WhatsApp API
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []
    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")
    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")
    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading
class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager
    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())
    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file
import threading
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
    def run_dashboard(self):
        threading.Thread(target=self.app.run, kwargs={'debug': True}).start()
```

gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox
class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard
    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)
        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")
        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        root.mainloop()
```

```python
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []
    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")
    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")
    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading
class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager
    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())
    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file
import threading
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
    def run_dashboard(self):
        threading.Thread(target=self.app.run, kwargs={'debug': True}).start()
```

gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox
class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard
    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)
        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")
        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        root.mainloop()
```

**whatsapp_api.py**
```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests

class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"

    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
        if response.status_code == 200:
            print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
        else:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")

    def receive_message(self):
        # Placeholder for receiving messages
        print("Listening for incoming messages...")
```

**database_manager.py**
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []

    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")

    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")

    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

```python
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file
import threading

class WebDashboard:

        self.app = Flask(__name__)

        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
```

```python
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem
```

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
        if response.status_code == 200:
            print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
        else:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
    def receive_message(self):
        # Placeholder for receiving messages
        print("Listening for incoming messages...")
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []
    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")
    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")
    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading
class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager
    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())
    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file
import threading
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
    def run_dashboard(self):
        threading.Thread(target=self.app.run, kwargs={'debug': True}).start()
```

gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox
class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard
    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)
        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")
        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        root.mainloop()
```

```python
Main entry point for the missed-call text-back solution.

from whatsapp_api import WhatsAppAPI
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem
from web_dashboard import WebDashboard
from gui_application import GUIApplication
def main():
    # Initialize components
    whatsapp_api = WhatsAppAPI()
    db_manager = DatabaseManager()

    # Start the GUI application
    gui_app.start()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
        if response.status_code == 200:
            print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
        else:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
    def receive_message(self):
        # Placeholder for receiving messages
        print("Listening for incoming messages...")
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []
    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")
    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")
    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading
class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager
    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())
    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file
import threading
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
    def run_dashboard(self):
        threading.Thread(target=self.app.run, kwargs={'debug': True}).start()
```

gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox
class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard
    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)
        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")
        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        root.mainloop()
```

main.py
```python
'''
Main entry point for the missed-call text-back solution.
'''
from whatsapp_api import WhatsAppAPI
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem
from web_dashboard import WebDashboard
from gui_application import GUIApplication

def main():
    # Initialize components
    whatsapp_api = WhatsAppAPI()
    db_manager = DatabaseManager()
    reply_system = AutomatedReplySystem(whatsapp_api, db_manager)
    dashboard = WebDashboard(db_manager, whatsapp_api)
    gui_app = GUIApplication(reply_system, dashboard)
    
    # Start the GUI application
    gui_app.start()
```

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests

class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"
    
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
        if response.status_code == 200:
            print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
        else:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")

    def receive_message(self, request_data):
        # Process incoming message data
        for entry in request_data.get('entry', []):
            for change in entry.get('changes', []):
                if change.get('field') == 'messages':
                    for message in change.get('value', {}).get('messages', []):
                        phone_number = message.get('from')
                        message_body = message.get('text', {}).get('body')
                        return phone_number, message_body
        return None, None
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []
    
    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")
    
    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")
    
    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading

class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager
    
    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())
    
    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file, request
import threading

class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager, whatsapp_api):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
        
        @self.app.route('/webhook', methods=['POST'])
        def webhook():
            phone_number, message_body = self.whatsapp_api.receive_message(request.json)
            if phone_number and message_body:
                self.db_manager.log_call(phone_number, datetime.datetime.now())
                self.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, "Thank you for your message. We will get back to you shortly.")
            return jsonify({'status': 'received'}), 200

    def run_dashboard(self):
        threading.Thread(target=self.app.run, kwargs={'debug': True}).start()
```

gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox

class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard
    
    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)
        
        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")
        
        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        
        root.mainloop()
```

 main.py
```python
'''
Main entry point for the missed-call text-back solution.
'''
from whatsapp_api import WhatsAppAPI
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem
from web_dashboard import WebDashboard
from gui_application import GUIApplication

def main():
    # Initialize components
    whatsapp_api = WhatsAppAPI()
    db_manager = DatabaseManager()
    reply_system = AutomatedReplySystem(whatsapp_api, db_manager)
    dashboard = WebDashboard(db_manager, whatsapp_api)
    gui_app = GUIApplication(reply_system, dashboard)
    
    # Start the GUI application
    gui_app.start()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

```python
'''

import requests

class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"
    
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
        if response.status_code == 200:
            print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
        else:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")

    def receive_message(self, request_data):
        # Process incoming message data
        for entry in request_data.get('entry', []):
            for change in entry.get('changes', []):
                if change.get('field') == 'messages':
                    for message in change.get('value', {}).get('messages', []):
                        phone_number = message.get('from')
                        message_body = message.get('text', {}).get('body')
                        return phone_number, message_body
        return None, None
```

```python
'''
Main entry point for the missed-call text-back solution.

from whatsapp_api import WhatsAppAPI
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem
from web_dashboard import WebDashboard
from gui_application import GUIApplication
def main():
    # Initialize components
    whatsapp_api = WhatsAppAPI()
    db_manager = DatabaseManager()

    # Start the GUI application
    gui_app.start()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
        if response.status_code == 200:
            print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
        else:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
    def receive_message(self, request_data):
        # Process incoming message data
        for entry in request_data.get('entry', []):
            for change in entry.get('changes', []):
                if change.get('field') == 'messages':
                    for message in change.get('value', {}).get('messages', []):
                        phone_number = message.get('from')
                        message_body = message.get('text', {}).get('body')
                        return phone_number, message_body
        return None, None
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []
    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")
    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")
    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading
class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager
    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())
    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file, request
import threading
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager, whatsapp_api):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
        @self.app.route('/webhook', methods=['POST'])
        def webhook():
            phone_number, message_body = self.whatsapp_api.receive_message(request.json)
            if phone_number and message_body:
                self.db_manager.log_call(phone_number, datetime.datetime.now())
                self.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, "Thank you for your message. We will get back to you shortly.")
            return jsonify({'status': 'received'}), 200
    def run_dashboard(self):
        threading.Thread(target=self.app.run, kwargs={'debug': True}).start()
```

gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox
class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard
    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)
        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")
        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        root.mainloop()
```

```python
def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
    if not phone_number or not message:
        print("Invalid phone number or message.")
        return
    
    headers = {
        "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
        "Content-Type": "application/json"
    }
    data = {
        "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
        "to": phone_number,
        "type": "text",
        "text": {
            "body": message
        }
    }
    
    try:
        response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
        if response.status_code == 200:
            print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
        else:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
    except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
        print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
```

```python
'''
Main entry point for the missed-call text-back solution.
'''
from whatsapp_api import WhatsAppAPI
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem
from web_dashboard import WebDashboard
from gui_application import GUIApplication
def main():
    # Initialize components
    whatsapp_api = WhatsAppAPI()
    db_manager = DatabaseManager()
    reply_system = AutomatedReplySystem(whatsapp_api, db_manager)
    dashboard = WebDashboard(db_manager, whatsapp_api)
    gui_app = GUIApplication(reply_system, dashboard)
    # Start the GUI application
    gui_app.start()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
        if response.status_code == 200:
            print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
        else:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
    def receive_message(self, request_data):
        # Process incoming message data
        for entry in request_data.get('entry', []):
            for change in entry.get('changes', []):
                if change.get('field') == 'messages':
                    for message in change.get('value', {}).get('messages', []):
                        phone_number = message.get('from')
                        message_body = message.get('text', {}).get('body')
                        return phone_number, message_body
        return None, None
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []
    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")
    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")
    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading
class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager
    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())
    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file, request
import threading
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager, whatsapp_api):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
        @self.app.route('/webhook', methods=['POST'])
        def webhook():
            phone_number, message_body = self.whatsapp_api.receive_message(request.json)
            if phone_number and message_body:
                self.db_manager.log_call(phone_number, datetime.datetime.now())
                self.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, "Thank you for your message. We will get back to you shortly.")
            return jsonify({'status': 'received'}), 200
    def run_dashboard(self):
        threading.Thread(target=self.app.run, kwargs={'debug': True}).start()
```

gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox
class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard
    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)
        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")
        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        root.mainloop()
```

"The code is generally well-structured and covers most of the requirements. However, the highest priority issue is the lack of error handling and validation, particularly in the `send_message` method of the `WhatsAppAPI` class. This method should include checks to ensure that the phone number and message are valid before attempting to send a message. Additionally, the method should handle potential exceptions from the `requests.post` call to prevent the application from crashing due to network issues or incorrect API usage.

**Suggestions for Revision:**
1. Add validation checks for phone number and message in the `send_message` method.
2. Implement try-except blocks to handle exceptions from the `requests.post` call.

Here's how you can revise the `send_message` method:

```python
def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
    if not phone_number or not message:
        print("Invalid phone number or message.")
        return
    
    headers = {
        "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
        "Content-Type": "application/json"
    }
    data = {
        "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
        "to": phone_number,
        "type": "text",
        "text": {
            "body": message
        }
    }
    
    try:
        response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
        if response.status_code == 200:
            print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
        else:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
    except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
        print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
```

Implementing these changes will improve the robustness and reliability of the application."

Here is a new customer's task: Please help me implement a Python program that uses a WhatsApp Business API to create a missed-call text-back solution that logs caller information, sends automated replies, stores call and message data with timestamps, supports message scheduling, and provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality..
To complete the task, you must write a response that appropriately solves the requested instruction based on your expertise and customer's needs.]

main.py
```python
'''
Main entry point for the missed-call text-back solution.
'''
from whatsapp_api import WhatsAppAPI
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem
from web_dashboard import WebDashboard
from gui_application import GUIApplication

def main():
    # Initialize components
    whatsapp_api = WhatsAppAPI()
    db_manager = DatabaseManager()
    reply_system = AutomatedReplySystem(whatsapp_api, db_manager)
    dashboard = WebDashboard(db_manager, whatsapp_api)
    gui_app = GUIApplication(reply_system, dashboard)
    
    # Start the GUI application
    gui_app.start()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests

class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"

    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        if not phone_number or not message:
            print("Invalid phone number or message.")
            return
        
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            if response.status_code == 200:
                print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
            else:
                print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"An error occurred: {e}")

    def receive_message(self, request_data):
        # Process incoming message data
        for entry in request_data.get('entry', []):
            for change in entry.get('changes', []):
                if change.get('field') == 'messages':
                    for message in change.get('value', {}).get('messages', []):
                        phone_number = message.get('from')
                        message_body = message.get('text', {}).get('body')
                        return phone_number, message_body
        return None, None
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []

    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")

    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")

    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading

class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager

    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())

    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file, request
import threading
import datetime

class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager, whatsapp_api):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.app = Flask(__name__)

        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})

        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)

        @self.app.route('/webhook', methods=['POST'])
        def webhook():
            phone_number, message_body = self.whatsapp_api.receive_message(request.json)
            if phone_number and message_body:
                self.db_manager.log_call(phone_number, datetime.datetime.now())
                self.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, "Thank you for your message. We will get back to you shortly.")
            return jsonify({'status': 'received'}), 200

    def run_dashboard(self):
        threading.Thread(target=self.app.run, kwargs={'debug': True}).start()
```

gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox

class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard

    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)

        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")

        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        root.mainloop()
```

```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests

class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"

    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        if not phone_number or not message:
            print("Invalid phone number or message.")
            return
        
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            if response.status_code == 200:
                print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
            else:
                print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"An error occurred: {e}")

    def receive_message(self, request_data):
        # Process incoming message data
        for entry in request_data.get('entry', []):
            for change in entry.get('changes', []):
                if change.get('field') == 'messages':
                    for message in change.get('value', {}).get('messages', []):
                        phone_number = message.get('from')
                        message_body = message.get('text', {}).get('body')
                        return phone_number, message_body
        return None, None
```

```python
class DatabaseManager:

        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})

    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")

    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()

                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

```python
'''
Main entry point for the missed-call text-back solution.
'''
from whatsapp_api import WhatsAppAPI
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem
from web_dashboard import WebDashboard
from gui_application import GUIApplication
def main():
    # Initialize components
    whatsapp_api = WhatsAppAPI()
    db_manager = DatabaseManager()
    reply_system = AutomatedReplySystem(whatsapp_api, db_manager)
    dashboard = WebDashboard(db_manager, whatsapp_api)
    gui_app = GUIApplication(reply_system, dashboard)
    # Start the GUI application
    gui_app.start()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        if not phone_number or not message:
            print("Invalid phone number or message.")
            return
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            if response.status_code == 200:
                print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
            else:
                print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
    def receive_message(self, request_data):
        # Process incoming message data
        for entry in request_data.get('entry', []):
            for change in entry.get('changes', []):
                if change.get('field') == 'messages':
                    for message in change.get('value', {}).get('messages', []):
                        phone_number = message.get('from')
                        message_body = message.get('text', {}).get('body')
                        return phone_number, message_body
        return None, None
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []
    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")
    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")
    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading
class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager
    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())
    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file, request
import threading
import datetime
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager, whatsapp_api):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
        @self.app.route('/webhook', methods=['POST'])
        def webhook():
            phone_number, message_body = self.whatsapp_api.receive_message(request.json)
            if phone_number and message_body:
                self.db_manager.log_call(phone_number, datetime.datetime.now())
                self.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, "Thank you for your message. We will get back to you shortly.")
            return jsonify({'status': 'received'}), 200
    def run_dashboard(self):
        threading.Thread(target=self.app.run, kwargs={'debug': True}).start()
```

gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox
class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard
    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)
        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")
        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        root.mainloop()
```

Based on the test report provided, the issue arises from the attempt to run a Flask application within a separate thread using `threading.Thread`. The error message indicates that the `signal` module, which is used internally by Flask's development server, can only be used in the main thread of the main interpreter. This is a common limitation when using Flask's built-in development server in a multi-threaded environment.

Here's a summary of the bugs causing the problem:

1. **Flask Development Server in a Thread**: The Flask application is being run inside a separate thread using `threading.Thread`. The Flask development server uses the `signal` module to handle termination signals, which is not compatible with running in a thread other than the main thread. This results in a `ValueError` when the server attempts to set up signal handlers.

2. **Use of Flask's Development Server**: The warning message indicates that the Flask development server is being used, which is not suitable for production environments. While this is not directly causing the error, it is important to note that a production-ready WSGI server should be used for deployment.

To resolve the issue, you should run the Flask application in the main thread. This can be done by modifying the `run_dashboard` method in the `WebDashboard` class to run the Flask app directly without using `threading.Thread`. Additionally, consider using a production-ready WSGI server like Gunicorn or uWSGI for deployment. Here's how you can modify the `run_dashboard` method:

```python
def run_dashboard(self):
    self.app.run(debug=True)
```

This change will ensure that the Flask application runs in the main thread, avoiding the `ValueError` related to signal handling.

```python
'''
Main entry point for the missed-call text-back solution.
'''
from whatsapp_api import WhatsAppAPI
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem
from web_dashboard import WebDashboard
from gui_application import GUIApplication
def main():
    # Initialize components
    whatsapp_api = WhatsAppAPI()
    db_manager = DatabaseManager()
    reply_system = AutomatedReplySystem(whatsapp_api, db_manager)
    dashboard = WebDashboard(db_manager, whatsapp_api)
    gui_app = GUIApplication(reply_system, dashboard)
    # Start the GUI application
    gui_app.start()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        if not phone_number or not message:
            print("Invalid phone number or message.")
            return
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            if response.status_code == 200:
                print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
            else:
                print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
    def receive_message(self, request_data):
        # Process incoming message data
        for entry in request_data.get('entry', []):
            for change in entry.get('changes', []):
                if change.get('field') == 'messages':
                    for message in change.get('value', {}).get('messages', []):
                        phone_number = message.get('from')
                        message_body = message.get('text', {}).get('body')
                        return phone_number, message_body
        return None, None
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []
    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")
    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")
    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading
class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager
    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())
    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file, request
import threading
import datetime
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager, whatsapp_api):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
        @self.app.route('/webhook', methods=['POST'])
        def webhook():
            phone_number, message_body = self.whatsapp_api.receive_message(request.json)
            if phone_number and message_body:
                self.db_manager.log_call(phone_number, datetime.datetime.now())
                self.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, "Thank you for your message. We will get back to you shortly.")
            return jsonify({'status': 'received'}), 200
    def run_dashboard(self):
        threading.Thread(target=self.app.run, kwargs={'debug': True}).start()
```

gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox
class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard
    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)
        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")
        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        root.mainloop()
```

Error Summary of Test Reports:
"Based on the test report provided, the issue arises from the attempt to run a Flask application within a separate thread using `threading.Thread`. The error message indicates that the `signal` module, which is used internally by Flask's development server, can only be used in the main thread of the main interpreter. This is a common limitation when using Flask's built-in development server in a multi-threaded environment.

Here's a summary of the bugs causing the problem:

1. **Flask Development Server in a Thread**: The Flask application is being run inside a separate thread using `threading.Thread`. The Flask development server uses the `signal` module to handle termination signals, which is not compatible with running in a thread other than the main thread. This results in a `ValueError` when the server attempts to set up signal handlers.

2. **Use of Flask's Development Server**: The warning message indicates that the Flask development server is being used, which is not suitable for production environments. While this is not directly causing the error, it is important to note that a production-ready WSGI server should be used for deployment.

To resolve the issue, you should run the Flask application in the main thread. This can be done by modifying the `run_dashboard` method in the `WebDashboard` class to run the Flask app directly without using `threading.Thread`. Additionally, consider using a production-ready WSGI server like Gunicorn or uWSGI for deployment. Here's how you can modify the `run_dashboard` method:

```python
def run_dashboard(self):
    self.app.run(debug=True)
```

This change will ensure that the Flask application runs in the main thread, avoiding the `ValueError` related to signal handling."
