'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file, request
import datetime
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager, whatsapp_api):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
        @self.app.route('/webhook', methods=['POST'])
        def webhook():
            phone_number, message_body = self.whatsapp_api.receive_message(request.json)
            if phone_number and message_body:
                self.db_manager.log_call(phone_number, datetime.datetime.now())
                self.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, "Thank you for your message. We will get back to you shortly.")
            return jsonify({'status': 'received'}), 200
    def run_dashboard(self):
        self.app.run(debug=True)

from whatsapp_api import WhatsAppAPI
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        if not phone_number or not message:
            print("Invalid phone number or message.")
            return
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            if response.status_code == 200:
                print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
            else:
                print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
    def receive_message(self, request_data):
        # Process incoming message data
        for entry in request_data.get('entry', []):
            for change in entry.get('changes', []):
                if change.get('field') == 'messages':
                    for message in change.get('value', {}).get('messages', []):
                        phone_number = message.get('from')
                        message_body = message.get('text', {}).get('body')
                        return phone_number, message_body
        return None, None
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []
    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")
    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")
    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading
class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager
    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())
    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file, request
import threading
import datetime
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager, whatsapp_api):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
        @self.app.route('/webhook', methods=['POST'])
        def webhook():
            phone_number, message_body = self.whatsapp_api.receive_message(request.json)
            if phone_number and message_body:
                self.db_manager.log_call(phone_number, datetime.datetime.now())
                self.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, "Thank you for your message. We will get back to you shortly.")
            return jsonify({'status': 'received'}), 200
    def run_dashboard(self):
        threading.Thread(target=self.app.run, kwargs={'debug': True}).start()
```

gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox
class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard
    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)
        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")
        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        root.mainloop()
```

Based on the test reports provided, the issue arises from the attempt to run a Flask application in a separate thread using the `threading.Thread` module. The error message indicates that the `signal` module, which is used internally by Flask's development server, can only be used in the main thread of the main interpreter. This is a limitation of the Python `signal` module, which does not allow signal handling in threads other than the main thread.

Here's a summary of the problem:

1. **Flask Application in a Separate Thread**: The `WebDashboard` class attempts to run the Flask application using `threading.Thread`. This causes a `ValueError` because the Flask development server uses the `signal` module, which is restricted to the main thread.

2. **Signal Handling Restriction**: The Python `signal` module can only be used in the main thread, and the Flask development server relies on this module for handling signals like `SIGTERM`.

To resolve this issue, you should run the Flask application in the main thread instead of using a separate thread. This can be done by modifying the `run_dashboard` method in the `WebDashboard` class to directly call `self.app.run()` without using `threading.Thread`. Alternatively, you can use a production-ready WSGI server like Gunicorn or uWSGI to run the Flask application, which does not have this restriction.

**[Seminar Conclusion]**:

 Based on the test reports provided, the issue arises from the attempt to run a Flask application in a separate thread using the `threading.Thread` module. The error message indicates that the `signal` module, which is used internally by Flask's development server, can only be used in the main thread of the main interpreter. This is a limitation of the Python `signal` module, which does not allow signal handling in threads other than the main thread.

Here's a summary of the problem:

1. **Flask Application in a Separate Thread**: The `WebDashboard` class attempts to run the Flask application using `threading.Thread`. This causes a `ValueError` because the Flask development server uses the `signal` module, which is restricted to the main thread.

2. **Signal Handling Restriction**: The Python `signal` module can only be used in the main thread, and the Flask development server relies on this module for handling signals like `SIGTERM`.

To resolve this issue, you should run the Flask application in the main thread instead of using a separate thread. This can be done by modifying the `run_dashboard` method in the `WebDashboard` class to directly call `self.app.run()` without using `threading.Thread`. Alternatively, you can use a production-ready WSGI server like Gunicorn or uWSGI to run the Flask application, which does not have this restriction.

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        if not phone_number or not message:
            print("Invalid phone number or message.")
            return
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            if response.status_code == 200:
                print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
            else:
                print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
    def receive_message(self, request_data):
        # Process incoming message data
        for entry in request_data.get('entry', []):
            for change in entry.get('changes', []):
                if change.get('field') == 'messages':
                    for message in change.get('value', {}).get('messages', []):
                        phone_number = message.get('from')
                        message_body = message.get('text', {}).get('body')
                        return phone_number, message_body
        return None, None
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []
    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")
    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")
    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading
class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager
    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())
    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file, request
import threading
import datetime
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager, whatsapp_api):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
        @self.app.route('/webhook', methods=['POST'])
        def webhook():
            phone_number, message_body = self.whatsapp_api.receive_message(request.json)
            if phone_number and message_body:
                self.db_manager.log_call(phone_number, datetime.datetime.now())
                self.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, "Thank you for your message. We will get back to you shortly.")
            return jsonify({'status': 'received'}), 200
    def run_dashboard(self):
        threading.Thread(target=self.app.run, kwargs={'debug': True}).start()
```

gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox
class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard
    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)
        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")
        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        root.mainloop()
```

"Based on the test reports provided, the issue arises from the attempt to run a Flask application in a separate thread using the `threading.Thread` module. The error message indicates that the `signal` module, which is used internally by Flask's development server, can only be used in the main thread of the main interpreter. This is a limitation of the Python `signal` module, which does not allow signal handling in threads other than the main thread.

Here's a summary of the problem:

1. **Flask Application in a Separate Thread**: The `WebDashboard` class attempts to run the Flask application using `threading.Thread`. This causes a `ValueError` because the Flask development server uses the `signal` module, which is restricted to the main thread.

2. **Signal Handling Restriction**: The Python `signal` module can only be used in the main thread, and the Flask development server relies on this module for handling signals like `SIGTERM`.

To resolve this issue, you should run the Flask application in the main thread instead of using a separate thread. This can be done by modifying the `run_dashboard` method in the `WebDashboard` class to directly call `self.app.run()` without using `threading.Thread`. Alternatively, you can use a production-ready WSGI server like Gunicorn or uWSGI to run the Flask application, which does not have this restriction."

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file, request
import datetime
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager, whatsapp_api):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
        @self.app.route('/webhook', methods=['POST'])
        def webhook():
            phone_number, message_body = self.whatsapp_api.receive_message(request.json)
            if phone_number and message_body:
                self.db_manager.log_call(phone_number, datetime.datetime.now())
                self.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, "Thank you for your message. We will get back to you shortly.")
            return jsonify({'status': 'received'}), 200
    def run_dashboard(self):
        self.app.run(debug=True)
```

Explanation: The `run_dashboard` method in the `WebDashboard` class was modified to directly call `self.app.run(debug=True)` instead of using `threading.Thread`. This resolves the issue with the Python `signal` module, which can only be used in the main thread.

'''
Main entry point for the missed-call text-back solution.
'''
from whatsapp_api import WhatsAppAPI
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem
from web_dashboard import WebDashboard
from gui_application import GUIApplication
def main():
    # Initialize components
    whatsapp_api = WhatsAppAPI()
    db_manager = DatabaseManager()
    reply_system = AutomatedReplySystem(whatsapp_api, db_manager)
    dashboard = WebDashboard(db_manager, whatsapp_api)
    gui_app = GUIApplication(reply_system, dashboard)
    # Start the GUI application
    gui_app.start()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        if not phone_number or not message:
            print("Invalid phone number or message.")
            return
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            if response.status_code == 200:
                print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
            else:
                print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
    def receive_message(self, request_data):
        # Process incoming message data
        for entry in request_data.get('entry', []):
            for change in entry.get('changes', []):
                if change.get('field') == 'messages':
                    for message in change.get('value', {}).get('messages', []):
                        phone_number = message.get('from')
                        message_body = message.get('text', {}).get('body')
                        return phone_number, message_body
        return None, None
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []
    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")
    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")
    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading
class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager
    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())
    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file, request
import datetime
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager, whatsapp_api):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
        @self.app.route('/webhook', methods=['POST'])
        def webhook():
            phone_number, message_body = self.whatsapp_api.receive_message(request.json)
            if phone_number and message_body:
                self.db_manager.log_call(phone_number, datetime.datetime.now())
                self.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, "Thank you for your message. We will get back to you shortly.")
            return jsonify({'status': 'received'}), 200
    def run_dashboard(self):
        self.app.run(debug=True)
```

gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox
class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard
    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)
        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")
        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        root.mainloop()
```

'''
Main entry point for the missed-call text-back solution.
'''
from whatsapp_api import WhatsAppAPI
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem
from web_dashboard import WebDashboard
from gui_application import GUIApplication
def main():
    # Initialize components
    whatsapp_api = WhatsAppAPI()
    db_manager = DatabaseManager()

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        if not phone_number or not message:
            print("Invalid phone number or message.")
            return
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            if response.status_code == 200:
                print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
            else:
                print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
    def receive_message(self, request_data):
        # Process incoming message data
        for entry in request_data.get('entry', []):
            for change in entry.get('changes', []):
                if change.get('field') == 'messages':
                    for message in change.get('value', {}).get('messages', []):
                        phone_number = message.get('from')
                        message_body = message.get('text', {}).get('body')
                        return phone_number, message_body
        return None, None
```
database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []
    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")
    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")
    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```
automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading
class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager
    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())
    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```
web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file, request
import datetime
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager, whatsapp_api):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
        @self.app.route('/webhook', methods=['POST'])
        def webhook():
            phone_number, message_body = self.whatsapp_api.receive_message(request.json)
            if phone_number and message_body:
                self.db_manager.log_call(phone_number, datetime.datetime.now())
                self.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, "Thank you for your message. We will get back to you shortly.")
            return jsonify({'status': 'received'}), 200
    def run_dashboard(self):
        self.app.run(debug=True)
```
gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox
class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard
    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)
        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")
        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        root.mainloop()
```

from whatsapp_api import WhatsAppAPI
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
from automated_reply_system import AutomatedReplySystem

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Handles interactions with the WhatsApp Business API.
'''
import requests
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.api_url = "https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID/messages"
        self.access_token = "YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"
    def send_message(self, phone_number, message):
        if not phone_number or not message:
            print("Invalid phone number or message.")
            return
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.access_token}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": phone_number,
            "type": "text",
            "text": {
                "body": message
            }
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.api_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            if response.status_code == 200:
                print(f"Message sent to {phone_number}: {message}")
            else:
                print(f"Failed to send message: {response.status_code} - {response.text}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
    def receive_message(self, request_data):
        # Process incoming message data
        for entry in request_data.get('entry', []):
            for change in entry.get('changes', []):
                if change.get('field') == 'messages':
                    for message in change.get('value', {}).get('messages', []):
                        phone_number = message.get('from')
                        message_body = message.get('text', {}).get('body')
                        return phone_number, message_body
        return None, None
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages storing and retrieving call and message data.
'''
import csv
import datetime
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calls = []
        self.messages = []
    def log_call(self, caller_info, timestamp):
        self.calls.append({'caller_info': caller_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged call from {caller_info} at {timestamp}")
    def log_message(self, message_info, timestamp):
        self.messages.append({'message_info': message_info, 'timestamp': timestamp})
        print(f"Logged message: {message_info} at {timestamp}")
    def export_to_csv(self):
        with open('logs.csv', 'w', newline='') as csvfile:
            fieldnames = ['type', 'info', 'timestamp']
            writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
            writer.writeheader()
            for call in self.calls:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'call', 'info': call['caller_info'], 'timestamp': call['timestamp']})
            for message in self.messages:
                writer.writerow({'type': 'message', 'info': message['message_info'], 'timestamp': message['timestamp']})
        print("Exported logs to logs.csv")
```

automated_reply_system.py
```python
'''
Handles sending automated replies and scheduling messages.
'''
import datetime
import threading
class AutomatedReplySystem:
    def __init__(self, whatsapp_api, db_manager):
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.db_manager = db_manager
    def send_automated_reply(self, caller_info):
        message = "Thank you for your call. We will get back to you shortly."
        self.whatsapp_api.send_message(caller_info, message)
        self.db_manager.log_message(message, datetime.datetime.now())
    def schedule_message(self, phone_number, message, time):
        delay = (time - datetime.datetime.now()).total_seconds()
        threading.Timer(delay, self.whatsapp_api.send_message, args=[phone_number, message]).start()
        print(f"Scheduled message to {phone_number} at {time}")
```

web_dashboard.py
```python
'''
Provides a web dashboard with real-time logs and CSV export functionality.
'''
from flask import Flask, jsonify, send_file, request
import datetime
class WebDashboard:
    def __init__(self, db_manager, whatsapp_api):
        self.db_manager = db_manager
        self.whatsapp_api = whatsapp_api
        self.app = Flask(__name__)
        @self.app.route('/logs', methods=['GET'])
        def get_logs():
            return jsonify({'calls': self.db_manager.calls, 'messages': self.db_manager.messages})
        @self.app.route('/export', methods=['GET'])
        def export_logs():
            self.db_manager.export_to_csv()
            return send_file('logs.csv', as_attachment=True)
        @self.app.route('/webhook', methods=['POST'])
        def webhook():
            phone_number, message_body = self.whatsapp_api.receive_message(request.json)
            if phone_number and message_body:
                self.db_manager.log_call(phone_number, datetime.datetime.now())
                self.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, "Thank you for your message. We will get back to you shortly.")
            return jsonify({'status': 'received'}), 200
    def run_dashboard(self):
        self.app.run(debug=True)
```

gui_application.py
```python
'''
Provides a GUI application for user interaction.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox
class GUIApplication:
    def __init__(self, reply_system, dashboard):
        self.reply_system = reply_system
        self.dashboard = dashboard
    def start(self):
        self.dashboard.run_dashboard()
        root = tk.Tk()
        root.title("Missed Call Text-Back Solution")
        tk.Label(root, text="Phone Number:").grid(row=0)
        tk.Label(root, text="Message:").grid(row=1)
        phone_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        message_entry = tk.Entry(root)
        phone_entry.grid(row=0, column=1)
        message_entry.grid(row=1, column=1)
        def send_message():
            phone_number = phone_entry.get()
            message = message_entry.get()
            self.reply_system.whatsapp_api.send_message(phone_number, message)
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "Message sent!")
        tk.Button(root, text='Send Message', command=send_message).grid(row=2, column=1, pady=4)
        root.mainloop()
```

# LangChain

Building applications with LLMs through composability

Looking for the JS/TS version? Check out LangChain.js.

**Production Support:** As you move your LangChains into production, we'd love to offer more comprehensive support.

Please fill out this form and we'll set up a dedicated support Slack channel.

## Quick Install

`pip install langchain`

or

`conda install langchain -c conda-forge`

## 🤔 What is this?

Large language models (LLMs) are emerging as a transformative technology, enabling developers to build applications that they previously could not. However, using these LLMs in isolation is often insufficient for creating a truly powerful app - the real power comes when you can combine them with other sources of computation or knowledge.

This library aims to assist in the development of those types of applications. Common examples of these applications include:

```markdown
# Missed-Call Text-Back Solution

A comprehensive solution for managing missed calls via WhatsApp Business API, providing automated text-back responses, logging, scheduling, and a web dashboard for real-time monitoring and data export.

## Overview

This software is designed to enhance customer interaction by automatically responding to missed calls with text messages, logging caller information, and providing a user-friendly interface for managing interactions. It includes features such as message scheduling and a web dashboard for real-time logs and CSV export functionality.

## Main Features

- **Automated Replies**: Automatically sends a text message to missed call numbers.
- **Call and Message Logging**: Stores call and message data with timestamps for future reference.
- **Message Scheduling**: Allows scheduling of messages to be sent at a later time.

# Missed-Call Text-Back Solution

A comprehensive solution for managing missed calls via WhatsApp Business API, providing automated text-back responses, logging, scheduling, and a web dashboard for real-time monitoring and data export.

## Overview

This software is designed to enhance customer interaction by automatically responding to missed calls with text messages, logging caller information, and providing a user-friendly interface for managing interactions. It includes features such as message scheduling and a web dashboard for real-time logs and CSV export functionality.

## Main Features

- **Automated Replies**: Automatically sends a text message to missed call numbers.
- **Call and Message Logging**: Stores call and message data with timestamps for future reference.
- **Message Scheduling**: Allows scheduling of messages to be sent at a later time.
- **Web Dashboard**: Provides a real-time view of logs and the ability to export data to CSV.
- **GUI Application**: Offers a graphical interface for user interaction and message management.

## Installation

### Prerequisites

Ensure you have Python installed on your system. You can download it from [python.org](https://www.python.org/downloads/).

### Environment Setup

1. **Clone the Repository**: Clone the project repository to your local machine.
   ```bash
   git clone https://github.com/your-repo/missed-call-text-back.git
   cd missed-call-text-back
   ```

2. **Install Dependencies**: Use the following command to install the required Python packages.
   ```bash
   pip install -r requirements.txt
   ```

### Configuration

1. **WhatsApp Business API Setup**: 
   - Replace `YOUR_PHONE_NUMBER_ID` and `YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN` in `whatsapp_api.py` with your actual WhatsApp Business API credentials.

## Usage

### Running the Application

1. **Start the Application**: Run the main script to start the application.
   ```bash
   python main.py
   ```

2. **Access the Web Dashboard**: Open your web browser and navigate to `http://127.0.0.1:5000` to access the dashboard.

### Using the GUI Application

- **Schedule a Message**: Use the scheduling feature to set a future time for sending messages.
